6. 2023(10-12æœˆ) å·¥ç¨‹ç±» ç¡•å£« å…¨èŒ@bloomberg - ç½‘ä¸Šæµ·æŠ• - æŠ€æœ¯ç”µé¢  | ğŸ™ Negative ğŸ˜£ HardFail | åœ¨èŒè·³æ§½

   > ç”µé¢ï¼Œé¢˜æ˜¯LC 428 ï¼Œå› ä¸ºé¢è¯•å®˜ç”µè„‘æœ‰é—®é¢˜ï¼Œè€½è¯¯äº†äº›æ—¶é—´ï¼Œæœ€åæ—¶é—´ä¸å¤Ÿï¼Œåªè¦æˆ‘å†™deserializeçš„éƒ¨åˆ†ï¼Œæˆ‘ç”¨äº†BFSï¼Œä»£ç ï¼š
   >
   > public Node deserialize(String str) {         Scanner scanner = new Scanner(str);         String rootValue = scanner.nextLine();         Node root = new Node(rootValue);         List `<Node>` layer = new ArrayList<>();         layer.add(root);         while (scanner.hasNextLine()) {             String line = scanner.nextLine();             List `<Node>` next = new ArrayList<>();             String[] split = line.split("\\|", Integer.MAX_VALUE);             for(int i = 0; i < split.length-1; i++) {                 Node node = layer.get(i);                 String[] splitNode = split[i].split(" ");                 for(String s : splitNode) {                     if(!s.isEmpty()) {                         Node n = new Node(s);                         node.children.add(n);                         next.add(n);                     }                 }             }             layer = next;         }         return root;     }
   >

    > 5åˆ†é’Ÿè¿‡ç®€å†ç„¶åhackerrankåšé¢˜
    > étagéleetcodeé¢˜ï¼š
    > "A string is valid if all characters of the string appear the same number of times. It is also valid if we can remove just 1 character in the string, and the remaining characters will occur the same number of times. Given a string s, determine if it is valid. If so, return true, otherwise return false.
    >
    >
    > For example, if s=abc, it is a valid string because frequencies are {a:1,b:1,c:1} . So is s=abcc because we can remove one c and have 1 of each character in the remaining string. If s=abccc however, the string is not valid as we can only remove 1 occurrence of c. That would leave character frequencies of {a:1,b:1,c:2}."
    >
    > å¤§æ¦‚easy-mediumâ€â€â€Œâ€Œâ€Œâ€â€Œâ€â€Œâ€Œâ€â€â€Œâ€Œâ€â€â€â€â€Œâ€Œ levelï¼Ÿä½†æ˜¯æ¥¼ä¸»ä¸€å¼€å§‹æ€è·¯æƒ³é”™äº†ï¼ˆæƒ³åˆ°stack å»äº†ï¼‰å¯¼è‡´æœ€åå‡ åˆ†é’Ÿæ‰å®Œæˆç»æ€ã€‚ã€‚ã€‚

51. 2022(10-12æœˆ) MachineLearningEng ç¡•å£« å…¨èŒ@bloomberg - å†…æ¨ - Onsite  | ğŸ˜ Neutral ğŸ˜ AverageOther | åœ¨èŒè·³æ§½

    > ML position
    > 1) CODINGé¢˜â€¢            im_stream: A stream (generator) that produces IMPosts. Calling next(im_stream) will yield a new post.
    > â€¢            target_sender_id: a string, the sender_id of the user we want to get a context for
    > â€¢            window_size: The number of posts before and after the target post that should be included
    > â€¢             in the context.
    > â€¢            
    > â€¢            Returns: An iterable (anything we can iterate over) containing the posts from the first conversational context found in im_stream.
    >
    >
    > â€¢            A context consists of an "target post" sent by target_sender_id, plus the window_size posts immediately
    > â€¢            before and after the anchor post that were made in the same chatroom.
    >
    >
    > 2) ML é¢˜
    > Consider an equity trader who chats with other traders on an instant messaging app:
    > - She is in several chatrooms, exposed to various kinds of chatter:
    > news about the market (e.g, "Oil prices are spiking")
    > trade negotiations (e.g, "I want to buy Tesla stock")
    > relationship building (e.g., "Lovely weather!")
    > - When flooded with unread messages (e.g., after stepping away from her desk or if the incoming message volume is high):
    > she'd like an automated way to discover actionable unread posts
    > i.e.,â€â€â€Œâ€Œâ€Œâ€â€Œâ€â€Œâ€Œâ€â€â€Œâ€Œâ€â€â€â€â€Œâ€Œ posts in which people have indicated interest in buying/selling equities

    > 1 first question:
    > You are building a global trading platform. Your clients submit limit orders with a given time-to-live to a selection of banks, each of which has different trading hours. You want to ensure that at least one of the selected banks is available to fill the order at any given time.
    >
    > Design a function to test if the selected banks' collective trading hours cover the entire duration of the order without any gaps.
    >
    > bool canITradeNow(XXX)??
    >
    > 09:00-16:00 Royal Bank of Scotland
    > 11:00-17:00 Morgan Stanley

    > Let's suppose Bloomberg is sponsoring a coding competition at its New York and San Francisco offices.
    > We will have to fly the participants to either one of these two offices. Each office can only accommodate half of the participants.
    > The goal is to assign each participant to an office in a way that the total travel cost for the company is minimized.
    >
    > Each participant will be represented as a pair of costs: <costToFlyToNY, costToFlyToSF>.
    >
    >
    > Paâ€â€â€Œâ€Œâ€Œâ€â€Œâ€â€Œâ€Œâ€â€â€Œâ€Œâ€â€â€â€â€Œâ€Œrticipant List as <costToFlyToNY, costToFlyToSF>:

     > Question Description
     > You are building a global trading platform. Your clients submit limit orders with a given time-to-live to a selection of banks, each of which has different trading hours. You want to ensure that at least one of the selected banks is available to fill the order at any given time.
     > Design a function to test if the selected banks' collective trading hours cover the entire duration of the order without any gaps.
     > Sample inputs - Expected outputs
     > All the test cases use the following set of banks:
     > â€¢ ï»¿ï»¿09:00-16:00 Royal Bank of Scotland
     > â€¢ ï»¿ï»¿71:00-17:00 Morgan Stanley
     >
     > â€¢ ï»¿ï»¿14:00-20:00 JP Morgan
     > â€¢ ï»¿ï»¿02:00-07:00 National Australia Bank
     > Test case is order hours followed by a list of banks.
     > TRADE VALID or TRADE FAILED.
     > â€¢ ï»¿ï»¿Test case #1 - expected result: SUCCESS10:00-17:00
     > â€¢ ï»¿ï»¿Test case #2 - expected result: FAILURE15:00-21:00
     > â€â€â€Œâ€Œâ€Œâ€â€Œâ€â€Œâ€Œâ€â€â€Œâ€Œâ€â€â€â€â€Œâ€Œâ€¢ ï»¿ï»¿Test case #3 - expected result: FAILURE04:00-10:00
     > These test cases do not include wrapped bank or order hours

264. 2023(7-9æœˆ) ç å†œç±»General ç¡•å£« å…¨èŒ@bloomberg - ç½‘ä¸Šæµ·æŠ• - æŠ€æœ¯ç”µé¢  | ğŸ˜ƒ Positive ğŸ™‚ EasyPass | åº”å±Šæ¯•ä¸šç”Ÿ

     > 2. BQ:

     > (1) ä¸è®°å¾—åˆ©å£é¢˜å·ï¼Œä½†åŸé¢˜å¯è§: ğŸ”— www.geeksforgeeks.org
     > (2) åˆ©å£ ä¼é¶é¢† (OOD) Lottery System: ğŸ”— leetcode.com
     > 4. åå‘BQ

     > æ±‚åŠ ç±³ï¼Œéå¸¸æ„Ÿè°¢ï¼

     > è¡¥å……å†…å®¹ (2022-09-01 02:19 +8:00):
     > æŠ±æ­‰ç¬¬ä¸€é¢˜è´´é”™é¢˜äº†ï¼Œæˆ‘æ²¡åœ¨åˆ©å£ä¸­æ‰¾åˆ°åŸé¢˜ï¼Œä½†æ‰¾åˆ°å‡ ä¹ä¸€æ ·çš„ï¼š
     > åˆ©å£å¹ºæ•£å˜¶è€Œï¼Œå”¯ä¸€çš„ä¸åŒæ˜¯ if num is odd, 3 * num + 1.
     > e.g. 5 -> 16 -> 8 -> 4 -> 2 -> 1, return 5 steps in total.
     > å¦å¤–è¿™é¢˜è¿˜æœ‰ä¸ªfollow upé—®é¢˜å¿˜æäº†ï¼šå¦‚æœå¤§é‡åœ°callè¿™ä¸ªAPIï¼Œæ˜¯å¦å¯ä»¥ä¼˜åŒ–time complexity (å…ˆè®²æ€è·¯ç„¶åimplement in code)ï¼Ÿ
     > æˆ‘çš„solution:
     > 1. Maintain a current HashMap to store the results in each call, e.g. {{5, 5}, {16, 4}, {8, 3}... }
     > 2. Before ending each call, put all the results in the current HashMap into a global HashMap, e.g {{5, 5}, {16, 4}, {8, 3}..., {2000, 302}, â€â€â€Œâ€Œâ€Œâ€â€Œâ€â€Œâ€Œâ€â€â€Œâ€Œâ€â€â€â€â€Œâ€Œ...}.
     > 3. For the following calls, if during the calculation of steps, we find out the current num is in the global HashMap, then we "return globalMap.get(num) + steps" directly.

     > æ€»è§‰å¾—å¯èƒ½head countæ»¡äº†ï¼Œå‡ºé¢˜æ–¹å¼çœŸçš„éå…¸å‹ã€‚è€Œä¸”é¢è¯•å®˜æ—¶å¸¸åœ¨æˆ‘å›ç­”åˆ°ä¸€åŠçš„æ—¶å€™ï¼Œæ›´æ”¹å·²ç»ç¡®è®¤å¥½çš„spec/requirementï¼Œæœ‰ç‚¹æƒ³è¦åˆ»æ„æ‰¾ç†ç”±failäººã€‚
     >
     > å½“ç„¶ï¼Œå¦å¤–ä¸€æ–¹é¢ï¼Œå¯èƒ½æ˜¯æˆ‘æœ‰äº›åœ°æ–¹æ¯”è¾ƒæ²¡ç»éªŒï¼Œä»–ä»¬è¿˜æ˜¯ä¸ä¿¡ä»»æˆ‘èƒ½èƒœä»»ã€‚å› æ­¤è¿™è¾¹æƒ³è¦è¯·æ•™ã€‚ç‰¹åˆ«æ˜¯multithreadingï¼Œå’Œç³»ç»Ÿè®¾è®¡ä¸Šé¢ã€‚è°¢è°¢
     >
     > anywayï¼Œè¿˜æ˜¯å¾ˆæ„Ÿè°¢å¼€èŠ±å ¡ç»™æœºä¼šï¼Œç»™æˆ‘é¢äº†ä¸¤ä¸ªèŒä½ã€‚è¿™æ˜¯æˆ‘åœ¨ç±³å›½æ±‚èŒä»¥æ¥ï¼Œç¬¬ä¸€ä¸ªå¤§å‚çš„onsiteã€‚
     >
     >
     > 1. First Round of Tech Interview ï¼ˆå…©ä½æ­æ´²äººï¼‰
     >
     > ä»¥ä¸‹å†…å®¹éœ€è¦ç§¯åˆ†é«˜äº 200 æ‚¨å·²ç»å¯ä»¥æµè§ˆ
     >
     > 1) self introduction
     >
     > 2) questions
     > Implement the function:
     > def merge_files(file1, file2, output_file)
     > Where file1 and file2 are filepaths and the function will read the two files
     > and merge the contents and output into output_file
     >
     > File 1:
     > id n  B  A
     > ID1|2|D1|D2
     > ID2|2|D1|D2
     > ID3|2|D1|D2
     > ID40000000|2|D1|D2
     >
     > File 2:
     > id n  C  D
     > ID1|2|D3|D4
     > ID3|2|D3|D4
     > ID4|2|D3|D4
     > ID5|2|D3|D4
     > ID6|2|D3|D4
     > .... x 1000000
     > ID40000000|2|D1|D2
     >
     >
     > Output File:
     > ID1|4|D1|D2|D3|D4
     > ID2|4|D1|D2|N.A|N.A
     > ID3|4|D1|D2|D3|D4
     > ID4|4|D1|D2|D3|D4
     > ID5|4|N.A|N.A|D3|D4
     > ID6|4|N.A|N.A|D3|D4
     >
     >
     > è¿™é¢˜å¾ˆå¦™ï¼Œåœ¨hackerrankä¸Šçš„ä»‹é¢åº”è¯¥æ²¡æœ‰åŠæ³•çœŸçš„ç»™ä¸€ä¸ªæ¡£æ¡ˆã€‚ç»“æœinputè¿˜æ˜¯ç”¨nested listæ¥åšã€‚
     >
     > æ­¤å¤–ï¼Œè¿™é¢˜ä¹Ÿä¸æ˜¯åœ¨åœ°é‡Œæˆ–æ˜¯leetcodeä¸Šæœ‰çš„ï¼Œæˆ‘ä¸€åº¦æ€€ç–‘æˆ‘æ˜¯ä¸æ˜¯åœ¨é¢data engineeringã€‚
     >
     > è¿™é¢˜é¢è¯•å®˜å‡†è®¸æˆ‘ç”¨pandasæ¥åšã€‚
     >
     > ä¹‹åfollow upå¦‚æœæ¡£æ¡ˆå¾ˆå¤§æ€ä¹ˆå¤„ç†ï¼Œæˆ‘è¯´load in chunk, process by chunkã€‚æˆ–æ˜¯MapRedueã€‚
     >
     > 
     >
     > 2. Second Round of Tech Interview ï¼ˆå…©ä½æ­æ´²äººï¼‰
     > ä»¥ä¸‹å†…å®¹éœ€è¦ç§¯åˆ†é«˜äº 200 æ‚¨å·²ç»å¯ä»¥æµè§ˆ
     >
     > 1) self introduction
     >
     > 2) question 1
     >
     > replace "a_library_call" with a service call
     >
     > library_call takes ~100 microseconds
     >
     > service call will take ~100 milliseconds
     >
     >
     > def a_service_call(x, y, i):
     >     pass
     >
     >
     > def a_bulk_service_call(reqs):
     >     for req in reqs:
     >         a_service_call(req.x, req.y, req.i)
     >
     > class Req:
     >     def __init__(self, x, y, i):
     >         self.x = x
     >         self.y = y
     >         self.i = i
     >
     >
     > class MyClass(object):
     >     def a_method(self, i):
     >         self.x = fee(self.x, i)
     >         self.y = fie(self.y, i)
     >         if (self.x > self.y): # only 1 in 1000
     >             self.x = queue.append(Req(self.x, self.y, i)).retrieve()
     >             # self.x = a_service_call(self.x, self.y, i) # 100 microseconds, service call takes 100 ms
     >         self.z = foe(self.x, i)
     >
     > for obj in objs: # len(objs) = 1,000,000
     >     queue = []
     >     obj.a_method(i)
     >
